              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=hard-hitting-contemp">hard-hitting-contemp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54570527-kav-xreadingsolacex?shelf=books-with-dark-themes">books-with-dark-themes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136466652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2425184165093699656"><i>
  <b>Book Bound Society Read</b>
</i><br/><br/><b>
  <i>trigger warnings: suicide, self-harm, depression</i>
</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I am not a darling. I am a girl ready to explode into nothing.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><i>Hold Still</i> is Nina LaCour's debut novel, a heartbreaking young-adult contemporary that follows Caitlin Madison's life over the course of a year following the suicide of her best friend, Ingrid. Ten years after the initial release of this novel, a beautiful new paperback edition of this novel has been released with a moving author's note from LaC</span>
  <span id="freeText2425184165093699656" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Book Bound Society Read</b>
</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>trigger warnings: suicide, self-harm, depression</i>
</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I am not a darling. I am a girl ready to explode into nothing.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><i>Hold Still</i> is Nina LaCour's debut novel, a heartbreaking young-adult contemporary that follows Caitlin Madison's life over the course of a year following the suicide of her best friend, Ingrid. Ten years after the initial release of this novel, a beautiful new paperback edition of this novel has been released with a moving author's note from LaCour, and edition so externally beautiful that it almost ties with the internal beauty of this heartbreaking novel that is also full of hope.<br /><br />LaCour does not shy away from exploring the realities of Ingrid's depression - her pain, her sadness, her hurt (both internal and external). Yet she also does not shy away from exploring Caitlin's journey - a journey of grief and loss and guilt, but also of joy and strength and hope.<br /><br />Somehow, the author expertly manages to stay sensitive to the girl who was in so much pain she felt she had to kill herself, but also to the girl who lost her best friend and cannot possibly understand why.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>the sun stopped shining for me is all...i am sad. i am sad all the time and the sadness is so heavy that i can't get away from it. not ever.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The words that came from Ingrid herself were so powerful and so moving, they captured the experience of existing in deep depression in a way that can only be described as perfect, despite the heartbreaking theme they deal with.<br /><br />Yet LaCour also develops Caitlin's journey and allows the reader to watch Caitlin grow from a girl who exists in a field of grief and loss to a girl who instills hope in the people around her.<br /><br />LaCour writes a heartbreakingly beautiful (and I say beautiful not to romanticize the issue, but to acknowledge how the author wove hope and joy into a story that dealt with such intense subject matter) and honest portrayal of a subject far too often ignored in society.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I was in high school and then I grew up and I wrote this novel...Though it's about a tragedy, hope and resilience are its heart. May they beat for you, loud and clear, and help you to understand that as painful as life can be, staying with us is worth it.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="2425184165093699656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_183348024" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183348024" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4844873-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299680097p2/4844873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183348024?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/4844873-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142416945" href="/book/show/7945878-hold-still">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183348024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13488946122994760266"><br/><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>This little line pretty much describes the book for me….<b>”part longing, part sorrow, part hope.”</b><br/><br/>Nina LaCour’s Hold Still shows individuals of all ages struggling with death, suicide, grief, and the big, dark, lonely, overwhelming hole that one can leave in our lives when they are gone. Our story revolves around two friends--one who committed suicide and one left behind trying to understand and deal with the loss.<br/><br/>Readers meet best friends Caitlin and Ingrid along with parents, teachers, f</span>
  <span id="freeText13488946122994760266" style="display:none"><br /><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br />This little line pretty much describes the book for me….<b>”part longing, part sorrow, part hope.”</b><br /><br />Nina LaCour’s Hold Still shows individuals of all ages struggling with death, suicide, grief, and the big, dark, lonely, overwhelming hole that one can leave in our lives when they are gone. Our story revolves around two friends--one who committed suicide and one left behind trying to understand and deal with the loss.<br /><br />Readers meet best friends Caitlin and Ingrid along with parents, teachers, friends—old and new, and more in this beautiful little book. A book filled with words, pictures, journal entries, passion and pain. We see Caitlin try to cope with her pain, find an outlet to express herself and her loss, and move on and find new loves and friends. Much of the journey sounded familiar to me and some of it felt a bit too arty and pretentious. BUT overall the emotions rang true with me. Everything from the “I-can’t-handle-this” feeling to the sweet little romance felt very real and raw to me.<br /><br /><b>“It isn’t the happy ending that Ingrid and I had dreamed up, but it’s all a part of what I’m working through. The way life changes. The way people and things disappear. Then appear, unexpectedly, and hold you close.”</b><br /><br />After closing this book, I couldn’t help wondering if we ever really know what goes on in someone’s head and heart. Can we see the pain behind the smiles? Maybe if we hold still, look, listen, and talk to each other. Maybe.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13488946122994760266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Rue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68964075-rue"><img alt="Rue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599372956p2/68964075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3198824176?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rue" href="/user/show/68964075-rue">Rue</a>

  <span id="freeText3064190444799409732" style="display:none"><b>"... I'll go wherever you go. Ingrid and Caitlin were best friends and one night, Ingrid told Caitlin that she is going to go wherever Caitlin goes, but by dawn, she committed suicide. Now Caitlin has to deal with a completely new life without her best friend. Finally she finds Ingrid's journal and gets a chance to learn about Ingrid's other side. When she find this journal, it helps guide her in making new friends, finding a first love and learning to deal with a life without Ingrid.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585114983i/29164627._SX540_.jpg" alt="6760d54f4cae5fce2f5a33d551feec77" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>"I tried to ignore the feeling that something good between us was changing."</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585114983i/29164628.jpg" alt="5dc8c5fc278d42ca847ea1ac19942477" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I feel like a tough cookie for not bawling my eyes out while reading.<br><i>Solid 3.5 stars</i>✨</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7373882-angela?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7373882-angela?shelf=books-library-owns">books-library-owns</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer259713088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9823022040253202142"><b>There are so many things that I want so badly to tell you but I just can't.</b><br/><br/>The first time I picked <i>Hold Still</i> up, I didn't finish it. I can't remember why or even how far I got into the book. It couldn't have been much at all, because this book was beautiful from the very first page.<br/><br/>I can't find the words to explain just how much I loved <i>Hold Still</i>. It's completely heartbreaking but still leaves you with hope.<br/><br/>The characters alone are enough to give this 5 stars. From Ingrid to Caitlin to Ms. Del</span>
  <span id="freeText9823022040253202142" style="display:none"><b>There are so many things that I want so badly to tell you but I just can't.</b><br /><br />The first time I picked <i>Hold Still</i> up, I didn't finish it. I can't remember why or even how far I got into the book. It couldn't have been much at all, because this book was beautiful from the very first page.<br /><br />I can't find the words to explain just how much I loved <i>Hold Still</i>. It's completely heartbreaking but still leaves you with hope.<br /><br />The characters alone are enough to give this 5 stars. From Ingrid to Caitlin to Ms. Delani to Taylor, each and every character is well-developed. And they're <i>real</i> - so real it's painful.<br /><br />From the beginning to the very last page, we get to see Caitlin's growth as a character, how she moves on from her best friend's suicide. <i>Hold Still</i> is a must read; I highly recommend it.<br /><br /><b>The sun stopped shining for me is all. The whole story is: I am sad. I am sad all the time and the sadness is so heavy that I can't get away from it. Not ever.</b></span>

    <a title="hayden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2995566-hayden"><img alt="hayden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598996671p2/2995566.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513391180?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="hayden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="hayden" href="/user/show/2995566-hayden">hayden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142416945" href="/book/show/7945878-hold-still">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who were underwhelmed by &lt;i&gt;Thirteen Reasons Why&lt;/i&gt;</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513391180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2003098648579346303"><i>Hold Still</i> surprised me. I went in expecting something good, but not great; emotionally heavy, but not emotionally affecting; a good way to pass the time, but nothing fulfilling. maybe it's because of this that I was so blown away.<br/><br/>this is my first Nina LaCour book, although I see her name around everywhere. I've heard great things about her other two books, but never really put two and two together and realized that this was by her, too. she's now on my authors-to-watch list, at a pretty high sp</span>
  <span id="freeText2003098648579346303" style="display:none"><i>Hold Still</i> surprised me. I went in expecting something good, but not great; emotionally heavy, but not emotionally affecting; a good way to pass the time, but nothing fulfilling. maybe it's because of this that I was so blown away.<br /><br />this is my first Nina LaCour book, although I see her name around everywhere. I've heard great things about her other two books, but never really put two and two together and realized that this was by her, too. she's now on my authors-to-watch list, at a pretty high spot.<br /><br /><i>Hold Still</i> is about Caitlin, a girl reeling in the suicide of her best friend, Ingrid, left to pick up the pieces after a curveball she never saw coming. one day after school, she finds Ingrid's journal under her bed and begins to reconstruct her best friend while also trying to move on. LaCour capture's Caitlin's struggle perfectly: the novel is a perfect combination of present struggles and memories she can't quite let go of.<br /><br />I wish this book achieved <i>Thirteen Reasons Why</i>'s success. (it's, quite frankly, much better.)</span>

<div id="review_1629932940" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1629932940" />
    <a title="Kelsey Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9764479-kelsey-marie"><img alt="Kelsey Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595768113p2/9764479.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1629932940?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelsey Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelsey Marie" href="/user/show/9764479-kelsey-marie">Kelsey Marie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9764479-kelsey-marie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1629932940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3907308533319339419">*****For my full review, go to <a href='http://darlingandcompany.blogspot.com/2016/05/hold-still-by-nina-lacour.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darling & Co.</a>*****<br/><br/>Hold Still is the 5th book I am reading for Mental Health Awareness Month and is a captivating book about a girl, Caitlin, who is trying to survive the death of her best friend, Ingrid, who killed herself at the end of sophomore year. Although the books starts slow, and I was questioning if I would like Caitlin as a character, about a third in, it picks up speed as Caitlin comes to terms with the death of her friend, and learns that life moves on.</span>
  <span id="freeText3907308533319339419" style="display:none">*****For my full review, go to <a href="http://darlingandcompany.blogspot.com/2016/05/hold-still-by-nina-lacour.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Darling &amp; Co.</a>*****<br /><br />Hold Still is the 5th book I am reading for Mental Health Awareness Month and is a captivating book about a girl, Caitlin, who is trying to survive the death of her best friend, Ingrid, who killed herself at the end of sophomore year. Although the books starts slow, and I was questioning if I would like Caitlin as a character, about a third in, it picks up speed as Caitlin comes to terms with the death of her friend, and learns that life moves on.<br /><br />It really took a bit for the book to get going. In the first bit of it, there isn't much conversation, just Caitlin's observations, and with her in a depression, it's not that...well, there's just not a lot going on. But once Caitlin starts to build a friendship with Dylan and open up to Taylor, the book really starts to move along. It brilliantly shows the stages of grief after suddenly losing someone to suicide.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3907308533319339419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4378839-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304352390p2/4378839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129249726?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/4378839-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4378839-sarah?shelf=too-painful-to-finish">too-painful-to-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129249726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16162755402459494112">I've suffered through the first 50 pages, bored out of my mind. Every page reads like the diary of someone with a very uneventful life. I get that the chick is having a hard time dealing with the suicide of her best friend, but she lacks any emotion. She's numb, but she's incredibly dull too. The book is a constant stream of 'I did this. I did that.' It's just dry and I can't get into it. I flipped through the rest of the book to see if maybe the writing got any better or more interesting, but i</span>
  <span id="freeText16162755402459494112" style="display:none">I've suffered through the first 50 pages, bored out of my mind. Every page reads like the diary of someone with a very uneventful life. I get that the chick is having a hard time dealing with the suicide of her best friend, but she lacks any emotion. She's numb, but she's incredibly dull too. The book is a constant stream of 'I did this. I did that.' It's just dry and I can't get into it. I flipped through the rest of the book to see if maybe the writing got any better or more interesting, but it's more of the same. <br /><br />I just can't justify wasting any more time reading this book because it's boring me to tears. I'm taking it back to the library.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UBHTU24nNfBbC4DyMEw0KZixEFTB3OUkn34Av4YonHvpgiJOSfcHrQgJ309ZibDUZb1cpa472r8icGOCy100AA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('z1vb67ZOZPl+R2EV6Cvn+oNjLl2s72JjgAp8mFs9SQh2yCr2kZ5WpC1FPqiB7mMHfm9irMMIXfg9BB+lFkjhcw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2889003.Nina_LaCour">About Nina LaCour</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2889003.Nina_LaCour"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1282077633p3/2889003.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4431027922589984637">Nina LaCour grew up in the San Francisco Bay Area. Her first job was at fourteen in an independent bookstore, and she has since worked in two others. She has tutored and taught in various places, from a juvenile hall to a private college. She now teaches English at an independent high school.<br/><br/>Of Hold Still, Nina says:<br/><br/>“This book is about loss, and it’s also about art. The loss part comes from a clas</span>
  <span id="freeText4431027922589984637" style="display:none">Nina LaCour grew up in the San Francisco Bay Area. Her first job was at fourteen in an independent bookstore, and she has since worked in two others. She has tutored and taught in various places, from a juvenile hall to a private college. She now teaches English at an independent high school.<br /><br />Of Hold Still, Nina says:<br /><br />“This book is about loss, and it’s also about art. The loss part comes from a classmate’s suicide. I didn’t know him well, but learning of his death remains one of the most profoundly sad and confusing events of my teenage years. The art part comes from my mother, a high school photography teacher. A girl in one of her student’s photographs inspired the character of Ingrid. While I was writing, I learned how to develop and print black-and-white photographs in a darkroom.”<br /><br />Nina lives in Oakland, California with her wife and their two cute cats. Visit her online at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.ninalacour.com">www.ninalacour.com</a>.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4431027922589984637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
